<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315361 id=\"116315361\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present the discovery of three quasar lenses in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey, selected using two novel photometry-based selection techniques. The J0941+0518 system, with two point sources separated by 5.46 arcsec on either side of a galaxy, has source and lens redshifts 1.54 and 0.343. Images of J2257+2349 show two point sources separated by 1.67 arcsec on either side of an E/S0 galaxy. The extracted spectra show two images of the same quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.10. SDSS J1640+1045 has two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.70 and fits to the SDSS and Pan-STARRS images confirm the presence of a galaxy between the two point sources. We observed 56 photometrically selected lens candidates in this follow-up campaign, confirming three new lenses, re-discovering one known lens, and ruling out 36 candidates, with 16 still inconclusive. This initial campaign demonstrates the power of purely photometric selection techniques in finding lensed quasars.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315363 id=\"116315363\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strong gravitational lensing serves as a unique probe into the distant universe (e.g. Treu &amp; Ellis <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>, and references therein). One can use lenses as cosmic telescopes to study, e.g. the properties of quasar hosts at high redshifts (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Anomalies in image positions and fluxes can be used to probe dark matter substructure in the lensing object (Mao &amp; Schneider <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Dalal &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Vegetti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Nierenberg et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Microlensing due to compact objects in the lens galaxy (see Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) can be used to study the inner structure of lensed active galactic nuclei (AGNs), enabling measurements of the accretion disc size (Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Motta et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and thermal slopes (Anguita et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Eigenbrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>) and the geometry of the broad line region (Braibant et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). With additional monitoring, one can use the delay between arrival of the images as a cosmological distance indicator (e.g. Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>; Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1997</a>; Tewes, Courbin &amp; Meylan <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Bonvin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Treu &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Unfortunately, this field of research is limited by the small number of known lenses. Since strong gravitational lensing requires such a close alignment of a distant source with a foreground lensing object, lensed quasars are rare objects. Oguri &amp; Marshall (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) estimate that, given an <em>i</em>-band limiting magnitude of 21, there are \u223c0.2 lenses per square degree, of which \u224820\u2009per\u2009cent are information-rich quads. Thus, the large footprints of wide-field surveys [e.g. the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS, York et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>), Dark Energy Survey (DES, Diehl et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), Kilo-Degree Survey (de Jong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), Panoramic Survey Telescope and Rapid Response System (Pan-STARRS, Chambers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>)] are essential for successful searches.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Previous systematic searches for strongly lensed quasars have predominantly explored samples of objects with spectroscopic data. The Cosmic Lens All Sky Survey (Browne et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>; Myers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) with the Jodrell-Bank VLA Astrometric Survey (King et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>) explored flat-spectrum radio sources, resulting in the discovery of 22 lenses. In the optical, Pindor et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) compared single- and double-component fits to spectroscopically confirmed quasars in SDSS to identify closely separated pairs as lens candidates. The SDSS Quasar Lens Search (Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) explored low-redshift (0.6\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a02.2) spectroscopically confirmed quasars, using a morphological selection to find small-separation candidates and a colour-based selection to find lenses that are deblended in SDSS imaging. More recently, More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) applied a similar method to the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey (Dawson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), expanding the SDSS spectroscopic searches out to higher redshifts.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To expand searches to include the footprints of new and upcoming wide-field surveys, photometry-based techniques have been developed. Ostrovski et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) use Gaussian Mixture Models to search the DES Y1A1 (Diehl et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) footprint using DES photometry with the Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer (Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) and VISTA Hemisphere Survey (McMahon et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) infrared bands. Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) used an artificial neural network classifier applied to blue, extended objects, and Lin et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) search for red galaxies with multiple blue neighbours in DES.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we present the discovery of three new strongly lensed quasars selected by two independent photometry-based techniques applied to the SDSS DR12 footprint: J0941+0518 at (RA, Dec.) = (09:41:22.5, +05:18:23.9), J1640+1045 at (16:40:18.2, +10:45:05.1), and J2257+2349 at (22:57:25.4, +23:49:30.4). The quasar images are separated by 5.46, 2.20, and 1.67\u2009arcsec, and correspond to sources at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.54, 1.70, and 2.11, respectively. We also present the blind re-discovery of the lens HS 2209+1914 at (RA, Dec.) = (22:11:30.3, +19:29:13.2) and provide AO-assisted images showing the presence of an Einstein ring. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>, we describe the follow-up of lens candidates, and in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>, we provide model fits to the three newly discovered lenses. Finally, we conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315369 id=\"116315369\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 CANDIDATE SELECTION AND FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Candidates were selected using two photometry-based methods described in Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu (PopMix, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and Agnello (OutlierSel, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), applied to SDSS-DR12 data. The methods produced lists of 59 and \u223c250 candidates, respectively, from which 21 and 36 were selected for imaging and spectroscopic follow-up. A complete discussion of candidate sample size with choice of cuts is given in the respective paper.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Candidates were observed using the Near-Infrared Camera 2 (NIRC2), the Echellette Spectrograph and Imager (ESI, Sheinis et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>), the OH-Suppressing InfraRed Imaging Spectrograph (OSIRIS, Larkin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>), and the DEep Imaging Multi-Object Spectrograph (DEIMOS, Faber et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) at Keck Observatory; the ESO Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera (EFOSC2, Buzzoni et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1984</a>) at the New Technology Telescope; and the Adaptive Optics Module and Goodman Spectrograph at the Southern Astrophysical Research Telescope. In this campaign, we observed 56 total candidates (Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), including three new lenses and one known lens, described below.</p>                        <a id=\"116315372\" scrollto-destination=\"116315372\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">List of all observed candidates along with their selection method, observing outcome, and lens and source redshift, if available.        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=116315373 id=\"116315373\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 SDSS J0941+0518</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J0941+0518 was identified both by the PopMix and OutlierSel methods. Additionally, the galaxy and one quasar image have spectra in SDSS which identify the sources as a galaxy and quasar, respectively. The galaxy spectrum is blended with the second quasar image spectrum and shows a C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> feature at the expected wavelength based on the other quasar image\u2019s redshift.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup></p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Images were obtained with the OSIRIS Imager on 2016 November 9 (Kbb filter, \u03bb<sub>cent</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02172\u00a0nm, bandwith 415\u00a0nm, plate scale 0.02 arcsec per pixel, 27 exposures of 30 s, 3 arcsec dithers). Spectra were obtained with ESI on 2016 November 19 (echellette mode, 0.75 arcsec slit, wavelength coverage 3900\u201310900 \u00c5, three 600 s exposures with dithers).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Images show two point sources separated by 5.4554\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0003\u2009 arcsec on either side of the lens galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). The spectra (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) are consistent with coming from the same object at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.54, based on the C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> lines. The galaxy spectrum with the Ca H and K, <em>G</em>-band, Mg b, and Na D lines gives <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.343. These values agree with the SDSS spectra which give <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.55 and <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.343.</p>                        <a id=\"116315377\" scrollto-destination=\"116315377\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/477/1/10.1093_mnrasl_sly043/3/m_sly043fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466118&amp;Signature=0AoB03rTANzWHSzZssq3rIIbwsKag5b3O4OhZRnUlIx2Qxx-I7b7Al6JqV5dmosMxq3TK7MZHR~ND1pwP39w1BZLURv-imnV-5fHoHrfryPFoD~hqSJGtxTiD8X8GA3s~zEzLn-dA1YuLPDYX-KutUaCkRewsA-gMJfClbyDqJATNQ69Zo-tMzHFDW0pmFJhiyDzmUAXOAMv2zNVL2KUZu75usn~lloELK2fVtUEYufPBgWSIbgeBd6S~-sH9kUlGQiwIgvgV1ABPfACreH4ByO4BpB2-34QYkPZkr2Diozgx3ODhIvP0s83Z6r058-Wfvxj7uvJyoH8h6BeUTDAIw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Top to bottom: SDSS postage stamps, SIE model fits, and SIE+fluxes model fits to the newly discovered lenses. AO-assisted images were obtained with NIRC2 on 2016 September 21 (narrow camera, Kp filter, \u03bb<sub>cent</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02124\u00a0nm, bandpass 351\u00a0nm, plate scale 0.01 arcsec per pixel). Two sets of three 120 s exposures were taken using a three-point dither pattern in addition to two 60 s acquisition exposures. Spectra were obtained with EFOSC2 on 2016 September 27 (Gr#13 grism, 1.2 arcsec slit, wavelength coverage 3685\u20139315 \u00c5, dispersion 5.54 \u00c5 per pixel).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Images show two point sources separated by 1.6701\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0036\u2009arcsec on either side of an E/S0 galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). The point sources correspond to the same quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.11, based on the Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> + O <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>], C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, and C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] lines.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=116315382 id=\"116315382\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 SDSS J1640+1045</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J1640+1045 was identified by the OutlierSel method and <em>Gaia</em> multiplet detection (Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> Spectra were obtained with DEIMOS on 2017 March 29 (1.0 arcsec slit, 600ZD grating, \u03bb<sub>cent</sub>\u00a0=\u00a07150 \u00c5, GG455 order-blocking filter, 360 s exposure time). The results show two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.70, based on the C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>], C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, and [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>] lines.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This object has not been followed up with AO-assisted imaging, so we obtained positions and fluxes by modelling seeing-limited images from Pan-STARRS and SDSS. Models consist of two point sources and a galaxy. The quasar images (resp. galaxy) dominate in bluer (resp. redder) bands, and the structural parameters of the lens are systematically affected by proximity with the brightest quasar image (appreciably across different bands). Thus, we choose a de Vaucouleurs profile for the surface brightness of the lens, perform the fit in separate bands, and list the weighted averages of positions and effective radius.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The model converges for the four reddest bands in each set of images, but fails to converge for the bluest images. We show the model fits and residuals for the Pan-STARRS image cutouts in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. Combining the fits for all SDSS and Pan-STARRS bands and setting the brighter Image A at the origin, we find the component positions to be (<em>x</em>, <em>y</em>)\u00a0=\u00a0(0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01, 0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02) arcsec (Image A), (1.80\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01, 1.36\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.06) arcsec (Image B), and (0.43\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04, 0.34\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03) arcsec (galaxy). The half-light radius of the galaxy is 1.1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 arcsec and the total integrated magnitudes are listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"116315386\" scrollto-destination=\"116315386\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/477/1/10.1093_mnrasl_sly043/3/m_sly043fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611466118&amp;Signature=MfN7cpFWHnWuMAXy0HP5nbouSe0uc1Zzlmq5Mc~0Imk3Ggi30ci8hmwMTX4VKbsDyc~lVyOpM0XYTxPOtnwyHF1uKvhPanw~wYpn6iQqeg7Jw76JOR9vCfXz5Ok8sQ4evup2zVn6dC1UNXIH1Wj29ZqeJqdZ-fQb0vvAqGLVZEgxKhIU59A7GbsL5DPpNSm-IyBfNL3Ac7c6Za3sm~J3ytpTK3I0wZiROa2SFb0r6xf0RPWNlNZYfmebIGrTa7m0IioniTvotUE666x9mBfPMd6MoxKJ-brVCXAgj-Ja-DbKkOwk~kU-i9ZNZ0w6Nhv46i7wnX4Xnf2YQ8opverpJQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Col 1: Pan-STARRS image cutouts of SDSS J1640+1045.  .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>SDSS-<em>g</em>\u00a0</td><td>18.91\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.13\u00a0</td><td>20.26\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.10\u00a0</td><td>19.87\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.30\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>SDSS-<em>r</em>\u00a0</td><td>18.59\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.08\u00a0</td><td>19.94\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.08\u00a0</td><td>19.15\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.14\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>SDSS-<em>i</em>\u00a0</td><td>18.19\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td><td>19.54\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.07\u00a0</td><td>18.40\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.08\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>SDSS-<em>z</em>\u00a0</td><td>18.17\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0</td><td>19.52\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.09\u00a0</td><td>17.78\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.09\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Pan-STARRS-<em>r</em>\u00a0</td><td>18.39\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.00\u00a0</td><td>19.91\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>19.09\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Pan-STARRS-<em>i</em>\u00a0</td><td>17.97\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>19.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>18.89\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Pan-STARRS-<em>z</em>\u00a0</td><td>17.85\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>19.35\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>18.56\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Pan-STARRS-<em>y</em>\u00a0</td><td>17.73\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>19.23\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>18.57\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/116315387\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=116315388 id=\"116315388\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-4>2.4 SDSS J2211+1929</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">During the 2016 search campaigns, we blindly re-discovered the lens SDSS J2211+1929, identified by the PopMix model selection (Williams et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). This object was originally discovered as part of the Hamburg Quasar Survey as HS 2209+1914 (Hagen, Engels &amp; Reimers <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>). This system is especially significant: due to its small image-separation, it is almost indistinguishable from a pair of point sources. Here, we show NIRC2 images obtained during the 2016 campaign on 2016 September 21. The same setup was used as for SDSS J2257+2349, but with three sets of three 120 s exposures and two additional 60 s acquisition exposures. Despite the complex point spread function (PSF) structure, an excess between the quasar images can be seen which we associate with the lens galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, left). A simple pairwise PSF subtraction, in which Image A is subtracted from Image B and vice versa, reveals the lens galaxy as well as an Einstein ring (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, right). These results show the importance of high-resolution imaging to securely identify lenses where modelling techniques such as those used for J1640+1045 are not feasible due to the small separation of the images.</p>                        <a id=\"116315390\" scrollto-destination=\"116315390\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" tab</a><a data-section=\"116315390\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/477/1/10.1093_mnrasl_sly043/3/sly043fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611466118&Signature=Gp8d18aMGjHUmG9WpwfyIATPeoFbsG3Ft0ikGxPTiYknzlypwOQWRQFk6~672rrCDsOvI3R7W7PvAo1eXSIMF4c8BT270c5kWWxR5nELXNBDQluVltFQ0wZ7qr3mJJi8UL3~Wwxluid~UKiGX3pysSZBzPFkkYrunlM66P8O7V1ZcTvmHVQYukmFF8a0YkGduNrXnVDPToz4EtGmdpAywsa1mDNP7souHFSdqZHCEpBv~HsIx5jRUUaQZgfxVbC1M0wT2GQXlhDDi~eZiuLtusG17wcVjm-7Vc9x8cSltkyQ8QCz7tw4-HWhvWIXTLxULyQvOyJy-oyZ9rSvo2b9NA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=116315390&ar=4935196&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sly043fig4.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">A PSF subtraction reveals the lens galaxy and an Einstein ring in the NIRC2 AO-assisted image of SDSS J2211+1929.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315391 id=\"116315391\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 LENS MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We used the <span class=\"small-caps\">lensmodel</span> package (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) to fit simple lens models to J0941+0518, J1640+1045, and J2257+2349. We adopt a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) model, with surface density given by <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\kappa = b/(2\\sqrt{(1-\\epsilon )x^2 + (1+\\epsilon )y^2})$|\u2060</span>, where <em>b</em> is the lens strength, and the axial ratio <em>q</em> is related to <em>\u03b5</em> by <em>q</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a0(1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>\u03b5</em>)/(1\u00a0+\u00a0<em>\u03b5</em>). Model parameters were fit using the <span class=\"monospace\">optimize</span> routine, which minimizes <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> by varying source and galaxy positions, source flux, lens strength <em>b</em>, ellipticity <em>e</em>\u00a0=\u00a01\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>q</em>, and position angle <em>\u03b8</em><sub>e</sub>. The 1\u03c3 errors are found by determining the parameters for which <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\chi ^2 = \\chi _{\\text{min}}^2 + 1$|\u2060</span>. Our observational constraints are the image and galaxy positions and fluxes found using a centroid algorithm and aperture photometry for J0941+0518 and J2257+2349, and the fits from Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.3</a> for J1640+1045. We fit a model without using image fluxes and one using fluxes with 20 per cent uncertainties since flux ratios can be affected by microlensing and differential extinction (e.g. Mao &amp; Schneider <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Falco et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>) as well as the combined effects of quasar variability and time delays. With fluxes omitted, we have four constraints from the image positions relative to the galaxy and are fitting for <em>b</em>, <em>e</em>, <em>\u03b8</em><sub>e</sub>, and source position. This is more free parameters than constraints and so we expect \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00. In this case, the fitted parameters give an idea of the correct values for the SIE model, but the errors do not hold as much meaning as those for the fits including the flux ratios.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The SIE fit to SDSS J0941+0518 infers a lens with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 2.88_{-0.66}^{+0.01}$|</span> \u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.37_{-0.21}^{+0.01}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = -28_{-1}^{+70}$|</span> deg. (measured E of N) with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a05.37\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22122</sup>. Critical lines and caustics are plotted on the images in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> with the inferred source position. Including a flux ratio of 1.41\u00a0\u00d7\u00a0(1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2) increased \u03c7<sup>2</sup> to 30.3, but the parameter constraints improved: <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 2.88_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.37_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$|\u2060</span>, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = -28.2_{-0.9}^{+0.9}$|</span> deg. The lens is in close proximity (&lt;0.5 arcsec) to eight other sources in SDSS imaging. McConnachie et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>) identify six of these objects, including the lens, as belonging to a compact group of galaxies. The additional contribution to the lens potential from the group could explain the large image separation and indicates the need for a more complex lens model.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For SDSS J1640+1045, we find <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.81_{-0.01}^{+0.40}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.16_{-0.36}^{+0.09}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = 0.6_{-1.0}^{+0.1}$|</span> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a08.79\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22125</sup>. Including image flux ratios gives <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.89_{-0.04}^{+0.04}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.20_{-0.03}^{+0.03}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = 0.55_{-0.04}^{+0.04}$|</span> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a07.93\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22125</sup>. This is a typical size of previously discovered quasar lenses in SDSS.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The model fit to SDSS J2257+2349 gives <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.79_{-0.03}^{+0.09}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.28_{-0.18}^{+0.08}$|\u2060</span>, and <em>\u03b8</em><sub>e</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0\u221234<sup>+2</sup> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a02.0\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22124</sup>. Here, the model only places an upper bound on the position angle. Constraining the flux ratio to be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$3.85\\pm 20\\,{per \\,cent}$|</span> results in a model with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.761_{-0.001}^{+0.001}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.357_{-0.003}^{+0.002}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = -31.7_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$|</span> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a033.6. These values agree with the orientation of the lens galaxy as seen in the right-hand panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> and the mass centroid from the fit matches the light centroid from the images.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315396 id=\"116315396\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We followed up 56 lensed quasar candidates selected by two photometry-based techniques, independently applied to the SDSS-DR12 data set, confirming three new lenses. AO-assisted images of J0941+0518 and J2257+2349 reveal two quasar images on either side of a lensing source, separated by 5.46 and 1.67\u2009arcsec, respectively. Spectra confirm each system is a lens with <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.54 and 2.11, respectively, and <em>z</em><sub><em>l</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.343 for J0941+0518. SDSS J1640+1045 has two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.70 with similar features, and the presence of the lens galaxy is secured by fits to multiband SDSS and Pan-STARRS images, where it is detected with high significance. We fit SIE models to the lenses and recover Einstein radii that are similar those of lenses in SDSS found in previous searches. With deeper data, one could apply more complex models, e.g. including external shear terms or deviations from the SIE density law, in order to better constrain the shape of the lens.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Most \u2018inconclusive\u2019 objects appear as two point sources in images, but do not show signs of a lens galaxy. These will require spectra to confirm if they are images of the same quasar, or, similar to the case of J2211+1929 (HS2209), deeper imaging with careful PSF subtraction. In future follow-up campaigns, a quick PSF subtraction can be used as a tool for quickly examining targets while at the telescope.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A non-negligible subset of candidates were revealed as single point sources in follow-up imaging. Their uncertain SDSS morphology was given by CCD \u2018blooming\u2019, which is common for bright sources and visible on some known lenses. Subsequent Pan-STARRS images, not available at the time of this campaign, were clearer at distinguishing between spurious candidates and systems with truly multiple images.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The discovery of these lenses demonstrates the importance of photometry-based selection techniques to complement previous lens searches. None of the lenses shown here, except J0941+0518, have spectra in SDSS and thus were not explored by previous searches. The case of J0941+0518 is surprising: despite having, coincidentally, a fibre spectrum of the bright quasar image and one of the lens galaxy and counter-image, it was missed by previous spectroscopic searches. With the aim of generating a more complete sample of lenses, photometry-based searches will play an important role in exploiting the potential of new and upcoming surveys without readily available spectroscopic data.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315401 id=\"116315401\" class=\"backfootnotegroup-title\" >Footnotes</h2>\r\n<div content-id=\"fn1\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn1\" class=\"end-note-link\">1</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">After this paper was submitted, we learned that Claude Cornen had independently found this lens and posted it on Galaxy Zoo, <a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"https://talk.galaxyzoo.org/#/boards/BHZ0000001/discussions/DGZ000167u?page=3\" target=\"_blank\">https://talk.galaxyzoo.org/#/boards/BHZ0000001/discussions/DGZ000167u?page=3</a></p></div></span></div><div content-id=\"fn2\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn2\" class=\"end-note-link\">2</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">This system was also confirmed, in mid-April 2017, by an independent search (C. Lemon, private communication and in preparation).</p></div></span></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315404 id=\"116315404\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">TT acknowledges support by the Packard Foundation through a Packard Research Fellowship and by the National Science Foundation through grant AST-1450141. Rojas, C E Rusu, A J Shajib, X Wang,  Discovery of three strongly lensed quasars in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey, <em>Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society: Letters</em>, Volume 477, Issue 1, June 2018, Pages L70\u2013L74, <a href=\"https://doi.org/10.1093/mnrasl/sly043\">https://doi.org/10.1093/mnrasl/sly043</a></p>\r\n        </div>\r\n\r\n    <div type=\"hidden\" value=\"mnrasl\" /> \n    </div>\n\r\n                    </div>\r\n                </div>\r\n            </div>\r\n            <div id=\"ContentTab\" class=\"content active\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315361 id=\"116315361\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present the discovery of three quasar lenses in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey, selected using two novel photometry-based selection techniques. The J0941+0518 system, with two point sources separated by 5.46 arcsec on either side of a galaxy, has source and lens redshifts 1.54 and 0.343. Images of J2257+2349 show two point sources separated by 1.67 arcsec on either side of an E/S0 galaxy. The extracted spectra show two images of the same quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.10. SDSS J1640+1045 has two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.70 and fits to the SDSS and Pan-STARRS images confirm the presence of a galaxy between the two point sources. We observed 56 photometrically selected lens candidates in this follow-up campaign, confirming three new lenses, re-discovering one known lens, and ruling out 36 candidates, with 16 still inconclusive. This initial campaign demonstrates the power of purely photometric selection techniques in finding lensed quasars.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315363 id=\"116315363\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strong gravitational lensing serves as a unique probe into the distant universe (e.g. Treu &amp; Ellis <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>, and references therein). One can use lenses as cosmic telescopes to study, e.g. the properties of quasar hosts at high redshifts (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Anomalies in image positions and fluxes can be used to probe dark matter substructure in the lensing object (Mao &amp; Schneider <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Dalal &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Vegetti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Nierenberg et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Microlensing due to compact objects in the lens galaxy (see Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) can be used to study the inner structure of lensed active galactic nuclei (AGNs), enabling measurements of the accretion disc size (Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Motta et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and thermal slopes (Anguita et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Eigenbrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>) and the geometry of the broad line region (Braibant et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). With additional monitoring, one can use the delay between arrival of the images as a cosmological distance indicator (e.g. Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>; Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1997</a>; Tewes, Courbin &amp; Meylan <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Bonvin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Treu &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Unfortunately, this field of research is limited by the small number of known lenses. Since strong gravitational lensing requires such a close alignment of a distant source with a foreground lensing object, lensed quasars are rare objects. Oguri &amp; Marshall (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) estimate that, given an <em>i</em>-band limiting magnitude of 21, there are \u223c0.2 lenses per square degree, of which \u224820\u2009per\u2009cent are information-rich quads. Thus, the large footprints of wide-field surveys [e.g. the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS, York et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>), Dark Energy Survey (DES, Diehl et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), Kilo-Degree Survey (de Jong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), Panoramic Survey Telescope and Rapid Response System (Pan-STARRS, Chambers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>)] are essential for successful searches.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Previous systematic searches for strongly lensed quasars have predominantly explored samples of objects with spectroscopic data. The Cosmic Lens All Sky Survey (Browne et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>; Myers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) with the Jodrell-Bank VLA Astrometric Survey (King et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>) explored flat-spectrum radio sources, resulting in the discovery of 22 lenses. In the optical, Pindor et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) compared single- and double-component fits to spectroscopically confirmed quasars in SDSS to identify closely separated pairs as lens candidates. The SDSS Quasar Lens Search (Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) explored low-redshift (0.6\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a02.2) spectroscopically confirmed quasars, using a morphological selection to find small-separation candidates and a colour-based selection to find lenses that are deblended in SDSS imaging. More recently, More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) applied a similar method to the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey (Dawson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), expanding the SDSS spectroscopic searches out to higher redshifts.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To expand searches to include the footprints of new and upcoming wide-field surveys, photometry-based techniques have been developed. Ostrovski et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) use Gaussian Mixture Models to search the DES Y1A1 (Diehl et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) footprint using DES photometry with the Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer (Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) and VISTA Hemisphere Survey (McMahon et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) infrared bands. Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) used an artificial neural network classifier applied to blue, extended objects, and Lin et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) search for red galaxies with multiple blue neighbours in DES.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we present the discovery of three new strongly lensed quasars selected by two independent photometry-based techniques applied to the SDSS DR12 footprint: J0941+0518 at (RA, Dec.) = (09:41:22.5, +05:18:23.9), J1640+1045 at (16:40:18.2, +10:45:05.1), and J2257+2349 at (22:57:25.4, +23:49:30.4). The quasar images are separated by 5.46, 2.20, and 1.67\u2009arcsec, and correspond to sources at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.54, 1.70, and 2.11, respectively. We also present the blind re-discovery of the lens HS 2209+1914 at (RA, Dec.) = (22:11:30.3, +19:29:13.2) and provide AO-assisted images showing the presence of an Einstein ring. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>, we describe the follow-up of lens candidates, and in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>, we provide model fits to the three newly discovered lenses. Finally, we conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315369 id=\"116315369\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 CANDIDATE SELECTION AND FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Candidates were selected using two photometry-based methods described in Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu (PopMix, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and Agnello (OutlierSel, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), applied to SDSS-DR12 data. The methods produced lists of 59 and \u223c250 candidates, respectively, from which 21 and 36 were selected for imaging and spectroscopic follow-up. A complete discussion of candidate sample size with choice of cuts is given in the respective paper.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Candidates were observed using the Near-Infrared Camera 2 (NIRC2), the Echellette Spectrograph and Imager (ESI, Sheinis et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>), the OH-Suppressing InfraRed Imaging Spectrograph (OSIRIS, Larkin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>), and the DEep Imaging Multi-Object Spectrograph (DEIMOS, Faber et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) at Keck Observatory; the ESO Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera (EFOSC2, Buzzoni et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1984</a>) at the New Technology Telescope; and the Adaptive Optics Module and Goodman Spectrograph at the Southern Astrophysical Research Telescope. In this campaign, we observed 56 total candidates (Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), including three new lenses and one known lens, described below.</p>                        <a id=\"116315372\" scrollto-destination=\"116315372\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">List of all observed candidates along with their selection method, observing outcome, and lens and source redshift, if available.        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=116315373 id=\"116315373\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 SDSS J0941+0518</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J0941+0518 was identified both by the PopMix and OutlierSel methods. Additionally, the galaxy and one quasar image have spectra in SDSS which identify the sources as a galaxy and quasar, respectively. The galaxy spectrum is blended with the second quasar image spectrum and shows a C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> feature at the expected wavelength based on the other quasar image\u2019s redshift.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup></p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Images were obtained with the OSIRIS Imager on 2016 November 9 (Kbb filter, \u03bb<sub>cent</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02172\u00a0nm, bandwith 415\u00a0nm, plate scale 0.02 arcsec per pixel, 27 exposures of 30 s, 3 arcsec dithers). Spectra were obtained with ESI on 2016 November 19 (echellette mode, 0.75 arcsec slit, wavelength coverage 3900\u201310900 \u00c5, three 600 s exposures with dithers).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Images show two point sources separated by 5.4554\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0003\u2009 arcsec on either side of the lens galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). The spectra (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) are consistent with coming from the same object at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.54, based on the C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> lines. The galaxy spectrum with the Ca H and K, <em>G</em>-band, Mg b, and Na D lines gives <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.343. These values agree with the SDSS spectra which give <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.55 and <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.343.</p>                        <a id=\"116315377\" scrollto-destination=\"116315377\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/477/1/10.1093_mnrasl_sly043/3/m_sly043fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466118&amp;Signature=0AoB03rTANzWHSzZssq3rIIbwsKag5b3O4OhZRnUlIx2Qxx-I7b7Al6JqV5dmosMxq3TK7MZHR~ND1pwP39w1BZLURv-imnV-5fHoHrfryPFoD~hqSJGtxTiD8X8GA3s~zEzLn-dA1YuLPDYX-KutUaCkRewsA-gMJfClbyDqJATNQ69Zo-tMzHFDW0pmFJhiyDzmUAXOAMv2zNVL2KUZu75usn~lloELK2fVtUEYufPBgWSIbgeBd6S~-sH9kUlGQiwIgvgV1ABPfACreH4ByO4BpB2-34QYkPZkr2Diozgx3ODhIvP0s83Z6r058-Wfvxj7uvJyoH8h6BeUTDAIw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Top to bottom: SDSS postage stamps, SIE model fits, and SIE+fluxes model fits to the newly discovered lenses. AO-assisted images were obtained with NIRC2 on 2016 September 21 (narrow camera, Kp filter, \u03bb<sub>cent</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02124\u00a0nm, bandpass 351\u00a0nm, plate scale 0.01 arcsec per pixel). Two sets of three 120 s exposures were taken using a three-point dither pattern in addition to two 60 s acquisition exposures. Spectra were obtained with EFOSC2 on 2016 September 27 (Gr#13 grism, 1.2 arcsec slit, wavelength coverage 3685\u20139315 \u00c5, dispersion 5.54 \u00c5 per pixel).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Images show two point sources separated by 1.6701\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0036\u2009arcsec on either side of an E/S0 galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). The point sources correspond to the same quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.11, based on the Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> + O <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>], C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, and C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] lines.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=116315382 id=\"116315382\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 SDSS J1640+1045</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J1640+1045 was identified by the OutlierSel method and <em>Gaia</em> multiplet detection (Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> Spectra were obtained with DEIMOS on 2017 March 29 (1.0 arcsec slit, 600ZD grating, \u03bb<sub>cent</sub>\u00a0=\u00a07150 \u00c5, GG455 order-blocking filter, 360 s exposure time). The results show two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.70, based on the C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>], C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, and [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>] lines.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This object has not been followed up with AO-assisted imaging, so we obtained positions and fluxes by modelling seeing-limited images from Pan-STARRS and SDSS. Models consist of two point sources and a galaxy. The quasar images (resp. galaxy) dominate in bluer (resp. redder) bands, and the structural parameters of the lens are systematically affected by proximity with the brightest quasar image (appreciably across different bands). Thus, we choose a de Vaucouleurs profile for the surface brightness of the lens, perform the fit in separate bands, and list the weighted averages of positions and effective radius.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The model converges for the four reddest bands in each set of images, but fails to converge for the bluest images. We show the model fits and residuals for the Pan-STARRS image cutouts in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. Combining the fits for all SDSS and Pan-STARRS bands and setting the brighter Image A at the origin, we find the component positions to be (<em>x</em>, <em>y</em>)\u00a0=\u00a0(0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01, 0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02) arcsec (Image A), (1.80\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01, 1.36\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.06) arcsec (Image B), and (0.43\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04, 0.34\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03) arcsec (galaxy). The half-light radius of the galaxy is 1.1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 arcsec and the total integrated magnitudes are listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"116315386\" scrollto-destination=\"116315386\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/477/1/10.1093_mnrasl_sly043/3/m_sly043fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611466118&amp;Signature=MfN7cpFWHnWuMAXy0HP5nbouSe0uc1Zzlmq5Mc~0Imk3Ggi30ci8hmwMTX4VKbsDyc~lVyOpM0XYTxPOtnwyHF1uKvhPanw~wYpn6iQqeg7Jw76JOR9vCfXz5Ok8sQ4evup2zVn6dC1UNXIH1Wj29ZqeJqdZ-fQb0vvAqGLVZEgxKhIU59A7GbsL5DPpNSm-IyBfNL3Ac7c6Za3sm~J3ytpTK3I0wZiROa2SFb0r6xf0RPWNlNZYfmebIGrTa7m0IioniTvotUE666x9mBfPMd6MoxKJ-brVCXAgj-Ja-DbKkOwk~kU-i9ZNZ0w6Nhv46i7wnX4Xnf2YQ8opverpJQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Col 1: Pan-STARRS image cutouts of SDSS J1640+1045. class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/116315387\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=116315388 id=\"116315388\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-4>2.4 SDSS J2211+1929</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">During the 2016 search campaigns, we blindly re-discovered the lens SDSS J2211+1929, identified by the PopMix model selection (Williams et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). This object was originally discovered as part of the Hamburg Quasar Survey as HS 2209+1914 (Hagen, Engels &amp; Reimers <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>). This system is especially significant: due to its small image-separation, it is almost indistinguishable from a pair of point sources. Here, we show NIRC2 images obtained during the 2016 campaign on 2016 September 21. The same setup was used as for SDSS J2257+2349, but with three sets of three 120 s exposures and two additional 60 s acquisition exposures. Despite the complex point spread function (PSF) structure, an excess between the quasar images can be seen which we associate with the lens galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, left). A simple pairwise PSF subtraction, in which Image A is subtracted from Image B and vice versa, reveals the lens galaxy as well as an Einstein ring (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, right). These results show the importance of high-resolution imaging to securely identify lenses where modelling techniques such as those used for J1640+1045 are not feasible due to the small separation of the images.</p>                        <a id=\"116315390\" scrollto-destination=\"116315390\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label an Einstein ring in the NIRC2 AO-assisted image of SDSS J2211+1929.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315391 id=\"116315391\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 LENS MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We used the <span class=\"small-caps\">lensmodel</span> package (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) to fit simple lens models to J0941+0518, J1640+1045, and J2257+2349. We adopt a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) model, with surface density given by <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\kappa = b/(2\\sqrt{(1-\\epsilon )x^2 + (1+\\epsilon )y^2})$|\u2060</span>, where <em>b</em> is the lens strength, and the axial ratio <em>q</em> is related to <em>\u03b5</em> by <em>q</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a0(1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>\u03b5</em>)/(1\u00a0+\u00a0<em>\u03b5</em>). Model parameters were fit using the <span class=\"monospace\">optimize</span> routine, which minimizes <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> by varying source and galaxy positions, source flux, lens strength <em>b</em>, ellipticity <em>e</em>\u00a0=\u00a01\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>q</em>, and position angle <em>\u03b8</em><sub>e</sub>. The 1\u03c3 errors are found by determining the parameters for which <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\chi ^2 = \\chi _{\\text{min}}^2 + 1$|\u2060</span>. Our observational constraints are the image and galaxy positions and fluxes found using a centroid algorithm and aperture photometry for J0941+0518 and J2257+2349, and the fits from Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.3</a> for J1640+1045. We fit a model without using image fluxes and one using fluxes with 20 per cent uncertainties since flux ratios can be affected by microlensing and differential extinction (e.g. Mao &amp; Schneider <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Falco et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>) as well as the combined effects of quasar variability and time delays. With fluxes omitted, we have four constraints from the image positions relative to the galaxy and are fitting for <em>b</em>, <em>e</em>, <em>\u03b8</em><sub>e</sub>, and source position. This is more free parameters than constraints and so we expect \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00. In this case, the fitted parameters give an idea of the correct values for the SIE model, but the errors do not hold as much meaning as those for the fits including the flux ratios.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The SIE fit to SDSS J0941+0518 infers a lens with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 2.88_{-0.66}^{+0.01}$|</span> \u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.37_{-0.21}^{+0.01}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = -28_{-1}^{+70}$|</span> deg. (measured E of N) with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a05.37\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22122</sup>. Critical lines and caustics are plotted on the images in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> with the inferred source position. Including a flux ratio of 1.41\u00a0\u00d7\u00a0(1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2) increased \u03c7<sup>2</sup> to 30.3, but the parameter constraints improved: <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 2.88_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.37_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$|\u2060</span>, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = -28.2_{-0.9}^{+0.9}$|</span> deg. The lens is in close proximity (&lt;0.5 arcsec) to eight other sources in SDSS imaging. McConnachie et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>) identify six of these objects, including the lens, as belonging to a compact group of galaxies. The additional contribution to the lens potential from the group could explain the large image separation and indicates the need for a more complex lens model.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For SDSS J1640+1045, we find <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.81_{-0.01}^{+0.40}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.16_{-0.36}^{+0.09}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = 0.6_{-1.0}^{+0.1}$|</span> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a08.79\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22125</sup>. Including image flux ratios gives <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.89_{-0.04}^{+0.04}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.20_{-0.03}^{+0.03}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = 0.55_{-0.04}^{+0.04}$|</span> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a07.93\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22125</sup>. This is a typical size of previously discovered quasar lenses in SDSS.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The model fit to SDSS J2257+2349 gives <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.79_{-0.03}^{+0.09}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.28_{-0.18}^{+0.08}$|\u2060</span>, and <em>\u03b8</em><sub>e</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0\u221234<sup>+2</sup> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a02.0\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u22124</sup>. Here, the model only places an upper bound on the position angle. Constraining the flux ratio to be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$3.85\\pm 20\\,{per \\,cent}$|</span> results in a model with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$b = 0.761_{-0.001}^{+0.001}$|</span>\u2009arcsec, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$e = 0.357_{-0.003}^{+0.002}$|\u2060</span>, and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\theta _e = -31.7_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$|</span> deg., with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a033.6. These values agree with the orientation of the lens galaxy as seen in the right-hand panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> and the mass centroid from the fit matches the light centroid from the images.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315396 id=\"116315396\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We followed up 56 lensed quasar candidates selected by two photometry-based techniques, independently applied to the SDSS-DR12 data set, confirming three new lenses. AO-assisted images of J0941+0518 and J2257+2349 reveal two quasar images on either side of a lensing source, separated by 5.46 and 1.67\u2009arcsec, respectively. Spectra confirm each system is a lens with <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.54 and 2.11, respectively, and <em>z</em><sub><em>l</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.343 for J0941+0518. SDSS J1640+1045 has two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.70 with similar features, and the presence of the lens galaxy is secured by fits to multiband SDSS and Pan-STARRS images, where it is detected with high significance. We fit SIE models to the lenses and recover Einstein radii that are similar those of lenses in SDSS found in previous searches. With deeper data, one could apply more complex models, e.g. including external shear terms or deviations from the SIE density law, in order to better constrain the shape of the lens.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Most \u2018inconclusive\u2019 objects appear as two point sources in images, but do not show signs of a lens galaxy. These will require spectra to confirm if they are images of the same quasar, or, similar to the case of J2211+1929 (HS2209), deeper imaging with careful PSF subtraction. In future follow-up campaigns, a quick PSF subtraction can be used as a tool for quickly examining targets while at the telescope.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A non-negligible subset of candidates were revealed as single point sources in follow-up imaging. Their uncertain SDSS morphology was given by CCD \u2018blooming\u2019, which is common for bright sources and visible on some known lenses. Subsequent Pan-STARRS images, not available at the time of this campaign, were clearer at distinguishing between spurious candidates and systems with truly multiple images.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The discovery of these lenses demonstrates the importance of photometry-based selection techniques to complement previous lens searches. None of the lenses shown here, except J0941+0518, have spectra in SDSS and thus were not explored by previous searches. The case of J0941+0518 is surprising: despite having, coincidentally, a fibre spectrum of the bright quasar image and one of the lens galaxy and counter-image, it was missed by previous spectroscopic searches. With the aim of generating a more complete sample of lenses, photometry-based searches will play an important role in exploiting the potential of new and upcoming surveys without readily available spectroscopic data.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315401 id=\"116315401\" class=\"backfootnotegroup-title\" >Footnotes</h2>\r\n<div content-id=\"fn1\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn1\" class=\"end-note-link\">1</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">After this paper was submitted, we learned that Claude Cornen had independently found this lens and posted it on Galaxy Zoo, <a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"https://talk.galaxyzoo.org/#/boards/BHZ0000001/discussions/DGZ000167u?page=3\" target=\"_blank\">https://talk.galaxyzoo.org/#/boards/BHZ0000001/discussions/DGZ000167u?page=3</a></p></div></span></div><div content-id=\"fn2\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn2\" class=\"end-note-link\">2</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">This system was also confirmed, in mid-April 2017, by an independent search (C. Lemon, private communication and in preparation).</p></div></span></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=116315404 id=\"116315404\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">TT acknowledges support by the Packard Foundation through a Packard Research Fellowship and by the National Science Foundation through grant AST-1450141. class=\"citation-links\"></div><div class=\"citation-links\"><div class=\"crossref-doi js-ref-link\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1051/0004-6361/201423633\" class=\"inst-open-url-holders\" data-targetId=\"10.1051%2F0004-6361%2F201423633\"> </span></div>\u00a0</div></div></div></div></div><div content-id=\"bib7\" data-legacy-id=\"bib7\"><div class=\"refLink-parent\"><span class=\"refLink\"><a name=\"jumplink-bib7\" href=\"javascript:;\" aria-label=\"jumplink-bib7\"></a></span></div><div class=\"ref false\"><div id=\"ref-auto-bib7\" class=\"ref-content \"><div class=\"mixed-citation citation\"><p class=\"mixed-citation-compatibility\"><span class=\"person-group\"><span class=\"name string-name\"><div "Scanned all subtables", "Table captions or footers": {"Overview": " class=\"chapter-para\">During the 2016 search campaigns, we blindly re-discovered the lens SDSS J2211+1929, identified by the PopMix model selection (Williams et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). This object was originally discovered as part of the Hamburg Quasar Survey as HS 2209+1914 (Hagen, Engels &amp; Reimers <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>). This system is especially significant: due to its small image-separation, it is almost indistinguishable from a pair of point sources. Here, we show NIRC2 images obtained during the 2016 campaign on 2016 September 21. The same setup was used as for SDSS J2257+2349, but with three sets of three 120 s exposures and two additional 60 s acquisition exposures. Despite the complex point spread function (PSF) structure, an excess between the quasar images can be seen which we associate with the lens galaxy (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, left). A simple pairwise PSF subtraction, in which Image A is subtracted from Image B and vice versa, reveals the lens galaxy as well as an Einstein ring (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, right). These results show the importance of high-resolution imaging to securely identify lenses where modelling techniques such as those used for J1640+1045 are not feasible due to the small separation of the images."}, "Status": "Complete", "Link": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/link_gateway/2018MNRAS.477L..70W/PUB_HTML", "Pandas format": {"Table 5": {"Action": "Processed via pandas", "Status": "Complete", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Skipping since duplicate": ""}}}, "Table 2": {"Action": "Processed via pandas", "Status": "Complete", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Table correctly loaded": "", "Lens Kind": "2", "Detection table": ""}, "Table map to MasterLens database": {"Dec [\u00b0]": "Dec. J.", "Wang, X."], "journal_name": "Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society", "type_of_reference": "JOUR", "abstract": "We present the discovery of three quasar lenses in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey, selected using two novel photometry-based selection techniques. The J0941+0518 system, with two point sources separated by 5.46 arcsec on either side of a galaxy, has source and lens redshifts 1.54 and 0.343. Images of J2257+2349 show two point sources separated by 1.67 arcsec on either side of an E/S0 galaxy. The extracted spectra show two images of the same quasar at z<SUB>s</SUB> = 2.10. SDSS J1640+1045 has two quasar spectra at z<SUB>s</SUB> = 1.70 and fits to the SDSS and Pan-STARRS images confirm the presence of a galaxy between the two point sources. We observed 56 photometrically selected lens candidates in this follow-up campaign, confirming three new lenses, re-discovering one known lens, and ruling out 36 candidates, with 16 still inconclusive.
